Hydrogen bonds, which occur between a hydrogen donor (like -OH or -NH groups) and an acceptor (such as oxygen or nitrogen atoms), facilitate highly directional and specific binding between the host and guest molecules. They contribute to the selectivity and affinity of the complex by guiding the guest into the host's binding site and stabilizing the assembled structure. Anion-π interactions involve the attraction between negatively charged anions and electron-deficient π-systems (such as aromatic rings with electron-withdrawing substituents). These interactions can enhance binding strength and specificity, especially in cases where the host contains electron-deficient aromatic surfaces designed to recognize particular anionic guests. Together, these non-covalent forces enable the reversible, yet stable, assembly of complex supramolecular architectures, underpinning functions such as molecular recognition, sensing, and catalysis in
